<main role=\"main\">\n        <!-- Secondary header starts -->\n<div class=\"secondary-header cf\" id=\"wd-secondary-header\">\n    <!-- Branded journal header starts -->\n<div class=\"big-branded\">\n\n    <div class=\"publication-name\" id=\"wd-pub-name\">\n\t<div class=\"publication-title\" itemprop=\"name\" itemid=\"periodical\">\n\t\t\t\t<!-- Journal image link tile starts -->\n<!-- Logo tile starts -->\n<a href=\"/journal/0004-637X\" itemprop=\"url\">\n    <img src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/8febf88b-d09c-11e5-b0b6-759f86a2008e/apj-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Astrophysical Journal\">\n</a>\n<!-- Logo tile ends -->\n<!-- Journal image link tile ends -->\n</div>\n\t\t</div>\n    <div class=\"partner-logos m-hide\" id=\"wd-partner-logos\">\n            <div class=\"partner-logo-alignment\">\n                <!-- Partner logo tile starts -->\n<a href=\"\" class=\"overlay-launch\">\n    <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/8a2230b8-d09c-11e5-b0b6-759f86a2008e/aas-2018.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The American Astronomical Society, find out more\">\n</a>\n<span class=\"overlay-set\">\n    <div class=\"tint-screen\"></div>\n    <div class=\"overlay-panel\">\n        <a title=\"Close\"  class=\"close-icon close-overlay\" tabindex=\"0\" role=\"button\" aria-describedby=\"close-icon-description\"><span class=\"icon-close\"></span></a>\n        <p id=\"close-icon-description\" class=\"offscreen-hidden\">Click here to close this overlay, or press the \"Escape\" key on your keyboard.</p>\n        <div class=\"overlay-img\">\n            <a href=\"\">\n                <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/8a2230b8-d09c-11e5-b0b6-759f86a2008e/aas-2018.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The American Astronomical Society, find out more\">\n            </a>\n        </div>\n        <div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The American Astronomical Society (AAS), established in 1899 and based in Washington, DC, is the major organization of professional astronomers in North America. Its membership of about 7,000 individuals also includes physicists, mathematicians, geologists, engineers, and others whose research and educational interests lie within the broad spectrum of subjects comprising contemporary astronomy. The mission of the AAS is to enhance and share humanity's scientific understanding of the universe.</p> <p><a href=\"https://aas.org/\">https://aas.org/</a></div>\n        <p class=\"ta-c mt-1 mb-2\"><a href=\"\"></a></p>\n    </div>\n</span>\n<!-- Partner logo tile ends -->\n\n<!-- Partner logo tile starts -->\n<a href=\"\" class=\"overlay-launch\">\n    <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/7ebd1b32-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n</a>\n<span class=\"overlay-set\">\n    <div class=\"tint-screen\"></div>\n    <div class=\"overlay-panel\">\n        <a title=\"Close\"  class=\"close-icon close-overlay\" tabindex=\"0\" role=\"button\" aria-describedby=\"close-icon-description\"><span class=\"icon-close\"></span></a>\n        <p id=\"close-icon-description\" class=\"offscreen-hidden\">Click here to close this overlay, or press the \"Escape\" key on your keyboard.</p>\n        <div class=\"overlay-img\">\n            <a href=\"\">\n                <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/7ebd1b32-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n            </a>\n        </div>\n        <div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The Institute of Physics (IOP) is a leading scientific society promoting physics and bringing physicists together for the benefit of all. It has a worldwide membership of around 50 000 comprising physicists from all sectors, as well as those with an interest in physics. It works to advance physics research, application and education; and engages with policy makers and the public to develop awareness and understanding of physics. Its publishing company, IOP Publishing, is a world leader in professional scientific communications.</p> <p><a href=\"https://www.iop.org\">https://www.iop.org</a></p></div>\n        <p class=\"ta-c mt-1 mb-2\"><a href=\"\"></a></p>\n    </div>\n</span>\n<!-- Partner logo tile ends -->\n\n<p></p>\n                </div>\n        </div>\n    </div>\n<!-- Branded journal header ends -->\n</div> <!-- end secondary-header -->\n<!-- Secondary header ends --><div class=\"da1-da2\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ScholarlyArticle\" id=\"page-content\">\n            <div class=\"da1 ta1 article-head\">\n                <!-- Start Eyebrow block, containing Surtitle and Labels -->\n<div class=\"eyebrow\">\n\t<!-- Start Collection Labels -->\n    <!-- End Collection Labels --> </div>\n<!-- End Eyebrow block -->\n\n<h1 itemprop=\"headline\" class=\"wd-jnl-art-title\">An Evaluation of 10 Lensing Models of the Frontier Fields Cluster MACS J0416.1-2403</h1>\n\n<p class=\"mb-0\">\n\t<span data-authors=\"\">\n\t\t<span itemtype=\"http://schema.org/Person\" itemprop=\"author\" class=\"nowrap\"><span itemprop=\"name\">J. href=\"/searchaaskeyword?source=aas&amp;type=kwd_sub&amp;code=11%2F7&amp;code_desc=galaxies%3A+clusters%3A+individual&amp;subkwd=MACS_J0416_1_2403&amp;subkwd_desc=MACS+J0416.1-2403\">\n\t\t\t\t(MACS J0416.1-2403)\n\t\t\t</a>; <a href=\"/searchaaskeyword?source=aas&amp;type=kwd_group&amp;code=2%2F46&amp;code_desc=gravitational+lensing%3A+strong\">gravitational lensing: strong</a></p>\n\t</div>\n<!-- Start Reprint Link -->\n\t<!-- End Reprint Link --><!-- Start Journal RSS feed -->\n                    <div class=\"jnl-notifications-wrapper jnl-notifications-wrapper--rss\">\n                        <a class=\"wd-jnl-rss\" href=\"/journal/rss/0004-637X\"><span\n                                class=\"icon-feed <span class=\"icon-newtab\">\n            </a></p>\n        </div>\n\n    <!-- End Email Alert -->\n<!-- End Email Alert --><!-- Start Citation Alert Link -->\n                        <p>\n<div class=\"jnl-notifications-wrapper\">\n    <a class=\"wd-jnl-email-alert\" href=\"https://myiopscience.iop.org/signin?origin=a0&return=https%3A%2F%2Fiopscience.iop.org%2Fmyiopscience%2Falerts%2Fsubscribe%3FarticleID%3D0004-637X%2F863%2F1%2F60\"><span\n            class=\"icon-alarm icon-alarm--jhp\"></span>Create citation alert</a>\n</div><!-- End Citation Alert Link -->\n                    </div>\n\t\t</div>\n    </div>\n    <!-- Article information ends -->\n<!-- Start Info top-->\n    <!-- end Info top --><div class=\"article-content\">\n\t<span id=\"articleId\" class=\"hide\">0004-637X/863/1/60</span>\n<!-- Start Abstract -->\n    <h2 id=\"artAbst\" class=\"collapse-blocked\">Abstract</h2>\n        <!-- Start article video abstract -->\n\t<!-- End article video abstract -->\n\t<div class=\"article-text wd-jnl-art-abstract cf\" itemprop=\"description\">\n             <P>Galaxy clusters can act as gravitational lenses and magnify the universe behind them, allowing us to see deep into the early universe. The <I>Hubble Space Telescope </I>Frontier Fields program uses six galaxy clusters imaged by <I>Hubble</I> to discover and study galaxies at <I>z</I>\u00a0~\u00a05\u201310. Seven independent teams developed lens models and derived magnifications for each galaxy cluster, based on positional and redshift constraints from the best available data at the time. In this work we evaluate 10 models for MACS J0416.1-2403 that were made public in 2015 by contrasting them with new spectroscopic redshifts that were measured in 2016. We developed an independent comparison method that uses the source plane root-mean-square as a metric of lensing model performance. Our analysis quantifies the ability of models to predict unknown multiple images. We examine the source plane scatter of multiply imaged systems and explore the dependence of the scatter on the location and the redshift of the background sources. The analysis we present evaluates the performance of the different algorithms in the specific case of the MACS J0416.1-2403 models.</P> </div>\n    <!-- End abstract -->\n<!-- Start Export citation and abstract tools -->\n\t<p>\n\t\t<small>Export citation and abstract</small>\n\t\t<span class=\"btn-multi-block\">\n\t\t\t<a href=\"/export?articleId=0004-637X/863/1/60&doi=10.3847/1538-4357/aacf8e&exportFormat=iopexport_bib&exportType=abs&navsubmit=Export+abstract\" class=\"btn btn-primary wd-btn-cit-abs-bib\" title=\"Export BibTex\">BibTeX</a>\n\t\t\t<a href=\"/export?articleId=0004-637X/863/1/60&doi=10.3847/1538-4357/aacf8e&exportFormat=iopexport_ris&exportType=abs&navsubmit=Export+abstract\" class=\"btn btn-primary wd-btn-cit-abs-ris\" title=\"Export RIS\">RIS</a>\n\t\t</span>\n\t</p>\n<!-- End Export citation and abstract tools -->\n<!-- Start AAS Related Links -->\n<div class=\"reveal-container reveal-closed reveal-plus-icon bdt-1 mt-2 mb-2 wd-jnl-art-article-aas-related-links\">\n  <div class=\"replica-h3 mt-0\">\n    <a href=\"#\" class=\"reveal-trigger\" data-reveal-label-alt=\"Hide related links\">Related links</a>\n  </div>\n  <div class=\"reveal-content\">\n    <div class=\"article-meta\"> \n      <ul>\n      \t<li><a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2018ApJ...863...60R\" target=\"_blank\">NASA ADS Record <span class=\"icon-newtab\"></span></a></li>\n      \t<li><a href=\"http://nedwww.ipac.caltech.edu/cgi-bin/nph-objsearch?refcode=2018ApJ...863...60R&search_type=Search \" target=\"_blank\">NED Objects <span class=\"icon-newtab\"></span></a></li>\n      \t<li><a href=\"http://simbad.u-strasbg.fr/simbad/sim-ref?querymethod=bib&simbo=on&bibcode=2018ApJ...863...60R\" target=\"_blank\">Simbad Objects <span class=\"icon-newtab\"></span></a></li>\n      \t<li><a href=\"/journal/0004-637X/page/About%20Related%20Links\" target=\"_blank\">About Related Links</a></li>\n      \t</ul>\n    </div>\n  </div>\n</div>\n<!-- Start info bottom -->\n    <!-- End info bottom -->\n<!-- Start article full text -->\n\t<div xmlns:book=\"http://api.iop.org/Book/1.0/\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" class=\"wd-jnl-art-full-text article-text\">\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjaacf8es1\" name=\"apjaacf8es1\">1.\u00a0Introduction</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>Strong gravitational lensing in massive galaxy clusters provides an opportunity to study both the physical properties of clusters and the highly magnified background universe behind them. Strong lensing analysis can directly inform estimates of the total (baryonic and dark matter) projected mass distributions of galaxy cluster cores (e.g., Richard et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib80\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib80\">2010a</a>; Sharon et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib89\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib89\">2014</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib88\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib88\">2015</a>; Zitrin &amp; Broadhurst <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib95\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib95\">2016</a>; Monna et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib70\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib70\">2017</a>; Mahler et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib65\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib65\">2018</a>); the high magnifications associated with strong lensing clusters facilitate both observations of the high-redshift (<em>z</em> ~ 6\u201311) magnified background universe (e.g., Kneib et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib56\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib56\">2004</a>; Richard et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib82\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib82\">2008</a>; Coe et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib21\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib21\">2013</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib20\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib20\">2015</a>; Bouwens et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib9\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib9\">2014</a>; Bradley et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib13\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib13\">2014</a>; Atek et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib3\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib3\">2015</a>; Salmon et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib86\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib86\">2017</a>) and zoomed-in studies of highly magnified galaxies around <em>z</em>\u00a0~\u00a02 (e.g., Jones et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib45\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib45\">2010</a>; Bayliss et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib6\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib6\">2011</a>; Livermore et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib62\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib62\">2015</a>; Johnson et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib44\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib44\">2017a</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib41\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib41\">2017b</a>). Strong lensing clusters have also been used to constrain cosmological parameters (e.g., Jullo et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib48\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib48\">2010</a>; Cao et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib16\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib16\">2015</a>; Maga\u00f1a et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib64\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib64\">2015</a>; Acebron et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib1\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib1\">2017</a>). The <em>Hubble Space Telescope</em> (<em>HST</em>) \u00a0has been transformative for strong lensing research, enabling most of the studies listed above.</p><p>The <em>Hubble</em> Frontier Fields (HFF; Lotz et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib63\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib63\">2017</a>) targets six massive galaxy clusters that are used as cosmic telescopes to observe the background universe (<em>z</em> ~ 5\u201310). Each of the galaxy clusters and parallel fields was observed with seven optical and near-infrared bands using the Wide Field Camera 3 (WFC3) and the Advanced Camera for Surveys (ACS) over 140 orbits each, for a total of 840 <em>HST</em> orbits. Follow-up observations from a variety of observatories both on the ground and in space have provided complementary data, including spectroscopic redshifts (<em>z</em><sub>spec</sub>), which allowed for precise lens models and the magnification measurements needed to study the background universe (e.g., Oesch et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib73\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib73\">2015</a>; Alavi et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib2\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib2\">2016</a>; Laporte et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib59\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib59\">2016</a>; McLeod et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib67\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib67\">2016</a>; Bouwens et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib10\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib10\">2017</a>; Livermore et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib61\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib61\">2017</a>; Yue et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib94\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib94\">2017</a>; Atek et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib4\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib4\">2018</a>; Kawamata et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib50\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib50\">2018</a>).<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaacf8efn1\">1</a></sup>\n\n</p><p>The Space Telescope Science Institute (STScI) contracted several lens modeling teams to compute lens models for each of the HFF clusters and make them available to the public. As part of this effort, the different teams collaboratively evaluated the robustness of the multiply imaged systems that were found in these data. Other than agreeing on a uniform set of constraints, each team worked independently from the other teams. In that, the HFF initiative presents us with a unique opportunity to compare different algorithms that were used to model the same cosmic lenses, the various assumptions used by the lensing teams, and to learn about systematics in lens modeling and the strengths of different algorithms. Comparison projects using simulated galaxy clusters (Acebron et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib1\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib1\">2017</a>; Meneghetti et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib68\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib68\">2017</a>) and HFF clusters (Priewe et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib78\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib78\">2017</a>) investigate the performance of the algorithms employed by the lensing modelers. Other projects contrasted lens model predictions with observations from strongly lensed supernovae (Rodney et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib84\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib84\">2015</a>; Kelly et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib55\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib55\">2016</a>; Rodney et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib85\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib85\">2016</a>; Treu et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib91\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib91\">2016</a>).</p><p>Since the beginning of the HFF program, several versions of the lens models have been computed by each team. With each new version the quantity of constraints has increased due to the deep <em>HST</em> observations, allowing for identification of faint multiply imaged systems of background sources. In addition, the quality of the constraints has improved with spectroscopic follow-up providing confirmation of the arcs, and importantly, spectroscopic redshifts (e.g., Jauzac et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib38\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib38\">2014</a>; Richard et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib79\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib79\">2014</a>; Treu et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib92\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib92\">2015</a>; Caminha et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib15\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib15\">2017</a>; Karman et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib49\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib49\">2017</a>; Mahler et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib65\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib65\">2018</a>).</p><p>The goal of this paper is to examine the predictive power of strong lensing models. We evaluate the 10 public HFF version 3 lens models for MACS J0416.1-2403, taking advantage of newly measured spectroscopic redshifts (Caminha et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib15\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib15\">2017</a>) that were not available at the time the lens models were computed. We investigate how the different algorithms perform in regions of the field of view where there were no constraints when the lens models were computed. We also check for any dependence of the root-mean-square (rms) scatter of the systems on the source spectroscopic redshifts. With the new data we can explore the predictive power of the lens models through the source plane scatter and image plane projections. This is important for future predictions made using these models, including the location of new multiple images of known or newly discovered lensed sources.</p><p>This paper is organized as follows. The importance of source redshifts in strong gravitational lens models, MACS J0416.1-2403, and the lens models available from HFF are described in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaacf8es2\">2</a>. In Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaacf8es3\">3</a>, we describe the lensing equation and the complexities of using the image plane scatter. Next, we discuss the methodology and results from the source plane and image plane projection analysis. Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaacf8es4\">4</a> examines the V4 models for MACS J0416.1-2403, which used the newly measured redshifts as constraints. A summary and conclusions are provided in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaacf8es5\">5</a>. We assume a flat cosmology with \u03a9<sub><em>M</em></sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.3, \u03a9<sub>\u039b</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.7, and <em>H</em><sub>0</sub>\u00a0=\u00a070 km s<sup>\u22121</sup> Mpc<sup>\u22121</sup>.</p></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjaacf8es2\" name=\"apjaacf8es2\">2.\u00a0Background</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><h3 id=\"apjaacf8es2-1\" name=\"apjaacf8es2-1\">2.1.\u00a0Strong Lensing Constraints</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>Strong lensing analysis relies on correct identification of sets of multiply imaged lensed sources (\"arcs\"). Modelers use several selection criteria to identify multiple images, including morphology, color, redshift, and expected lensing geometry. Deep, high-resolution observations increase the feasibility of finding arc candidates but come with an extensive cost in observational resources. These observations are crucial since both the accuracy and precision of the lens models improve with the use of more lensed galaxies, as has been shown by Richard et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib81\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib81\">2010b</a>), Johnson &amp; Sharon (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib42\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib42\">2016</a>), and Mahler et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib65\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib65\">2018</a>).</p><p>The main constraints in strong lensing come from the observed positions of these images. Additionally, the redshift of the lensed source provides the distance (assuming a cosmology), giving us three-dimensional information on the geometry of the system (Equation (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"eqnref\" href=\"#apjaacf8eeqn1\">1</a>)). Ideally, all of the multiply imaged systems that are used to constrain the model would have spectroscopic redshifts. This is not typically the case, due to the high observational cost of spectroscopic follow-up. As the community devotes more resources to spectroscopic follow-up observations, the data become more complete. In the cases in which spectroscopic redshifts are not available, lens modeling algorithms can treat redshifts as free parameters, increasing the flexibility of the models and thus increasing their uncertainty.</p><p>In the absence of spectroscopic redshifts, photometric redshifts can be used in the modeling process. Photometric redshifts are prone to systematic uncertainties, which can be reduced with information from multiple band-passes and deeper data, although catastrophic failures are possible. Nevertheless, photometric measurements can be implemented in the modeling process by using their posterior probability distributions as a prior for the free-redshift parameter of the lensed source.</p><p>An investigation of the systematics in strong gravitational lens modeling exploring the importance of using spectroscopic redshifts was done by Johnson &amp; Sharon (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib42\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib42\">2016</a>), who found that the rms scatter in the image plane improves when increasing the number of spectroscopic systems used in computing the lens models. Cerny et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib17\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib17\">2018</a>) investigated methods for treating the redshifts of multiple images in various galaxy clusters and the effects on the magnifications computed from the lens models. The systematic uncertainties due to a small fraction of spectroscopic redshifts, compared to a large fraction, were analyzed in the case of Abell 2744 (Mahler et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib65\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib65\">2018</a>), which was observed as part of the HFF program. The systematic effect on the retrieval of cosmological parameters from strong lensing models due to the different density profiles used by parametric lens models and the effect of redshifts were explored by Acebron et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib1\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib1\">2017</a>) using simulated galaxy clusters (Meneghetti et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib68\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib68\">2017</a>).</p><p>In this work we take advantage of the factor of two increase in the number of lensing constraints with spectroscopically confirmed redshifts to evaluate lens models of the HFF cluster MACS J0416.1-2403.</p></div><h3 id=\"apjaacf8es2-2\" name=\"apjaacf8es2-2\">2.2.\u00a0The Predictive Power of Lensing Models in Clusters of Galaxies</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>All strong lens models rely on lensing observables as constraints. A variety of predictions can be made from the computed models, including the locations of new multiple images of known or newly discovered lensed sources. The use of lens models to find background-source projections is standard practice by lens modelers as well as the rest of the community, particularly for the purpose of discovering new images of lensed background sources, which in turn can help provide new constraints for the lens models.</p><p>With a well-constrained lens model, the angular separation between images of the same source can be used to estimate \"geometric\" redshifts in the absence of spectroscopic redshift (e.g., Zitrin et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib98\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib98\">2014</a>; Chan et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib18\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib18\">2017</a>). In addition, model-predicted redshifts can be compared to independent photometric redshift estimates and help discriminate between degenerate photometric redshifts (e.g., Lam et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib58\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib58\">2014</a>; Diego et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib24\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib24\">2015a</a>; Cerny et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib17\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib17\">2018</a>).</p><p>Time delay can also be predicted by lens models. Since the travel time of light depends on its path between the source and the observer, different images of the same source are not contemporaneous. The arrival time difference, or time delay, between multiple images of the same source depends on the lensing potential and can be directly derived from a lens model. If the source is transient or variable in nature, the time delay can be observationally measured and compared to lens model predictions, e.g., supernovae (Kelly et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib54\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib54\">2014</a>; Oguri <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib76\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib76\">2015</a>; Sharon &amp; Johnson <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib90\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib90\">2015</a>; Diego et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib25\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib25\">2016a</a>; Jauzac et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib40\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib40\">2016</a>; Kelly et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib55\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib55\">2016</a>; Treu et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib91\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib91\">2016</a>; Rodney et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib83\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib83\">2018</a>) and quasars lensed by clusters (Inada et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib36\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib36\">2006</a>; Fohlmeister et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib30\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib30\">2007</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib31\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib31\">2013</a>; Dahle et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib22\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib22\">2013</a>; Sharon et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib87\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib87\">2017</a>).</p><p>Finally, the lensing magnification is seldom a direct observable. In most cases, one can predict and measure the <em>relative</em> lensing magnification between images of the same source. The only known exception thus far is observed standard candles such as Type\u00a0Ia supernovae, whose peak magnitudes can be known through calibration and thus their absolute magnification can be compared to model predictions (Rodney et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib84\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib84\">2015</a>).</p><p>In this paper, we focus on the ability of lens models to properly predict the source locations of lensed images. For assessment of the predicting power of magnification or time delay, the reader is referred to the publications listed above.</p></div><h3 id=\"apjaacf8es2-3\" name=\"apjaacf8es2-3\">2.3.\u00a0MACS J0416.1-2403</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>MACS J0416.1-2403 is a massive cluster at a redshift <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a00.397 identified in the MAssive Cluster Survey (MACS Ebeling et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib28\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib28\">2007</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib29\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib29\">2014</a>). It was suggested that it is a merging cluster (Mann &amp; Ebeling <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib66\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib66\">2012</a>) due to the double-peak profile of its bolometric X-ray luminosity. The Cluster Lensing and Supernova survey with <em>Hubble</em> (CLASH) has studied this cluster to constrain its mass distribution (Postman et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib77\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib77\">2012</a>). Using the CLASH <em>HST</em> images, Zitrin et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib97\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib97\">2013</a>) identified 70 multiple images of 23 background sources, which were used in the strong lensing analysis. This cluster was previously observed by <em>Spitzer</em> IRAC (PI R. Bouwens), <em>Chandra Space Observatory</em>, Jansky Very Large Array, Giant Meterwave Radio Telescope (Ogrean et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib74\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib74\">2015</a>), and Very Large Telescope spectroscopy (e.g., Grillo et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib33\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib33\">2015</a>; Balestra et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib5\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib5\">2016</a>). As part of the HFF program, MACS J0416.1-2403 was observed again by <em>HST</em> in early 2014 and late 2014. Some of the most recent work exploring MACS J0416.1-2403 includes joint X-ray and strong lensing analysis to investigate the dark matter distribution in the core of the galaxy cluster (Bonamigo et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib8\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib8\">2017</a>). Line-of-sight structure is relevant when performing strong lensing analysis because the lensing signal is sensitive to the total projected mass distribution (Bayliss et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib7\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib7\">2014</a>; D'Aloisio et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib23\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib23\">2014</a>). A study of line-of-sight structure effects on the strong lens modeling of MACS J0416.1-2403 was presented by Chiriv\u00ec et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib19\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib19\">2018</a>). Natarajan et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib71\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib71\">2017</a>) studied the dark matter substructure of MACS J0416.1-2403 by comparing lensing -inferred substructure to that of simulations.</p><p>With the deep <em>HST</em> imaging, hundreds of multiple images have been identified and spectroscopic redshifts have been measured in follow-up observations. In 2015, seven independent lensing teams computed lens models for MACS J0416.1-2403 with the positional and redshift constraints available at that time. This included 17 sources with confirmed <em>z</em><sub>spec</sub> (Jauzac et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib38\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib38\">2014</a>; Richard et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib79\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib79\">2014</a>; Treu et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib92\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib92\">2015</a>). In this analysis, we refer to the set of lensed images with spectroscopic redshifts available when the lens models were computed as the \"training set.\" In 2016, a new follow-up survey by Caminha et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib15\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib15\">2017</a>) increased the number of spectroscopic redshifts to 39 sources and updated some of the previously found redshifts. The lensed images (arcs) with new spectroscopic redshifts are referred to as \"new set\" in our analysis. Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaacf8et1\">1</a> has a summary of the number of background sources and the multiple images with spectroscopic redshifts for MACS J0416.1-2403. The distribution of the source spectroscopic redshifts (<em>z</em><sub><em>s</em></sub>) is shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaacf8ef1\">1</a>. We note that most of the new arcs have a higher redshift compared to the training set. Out of the spectroscopic redshifts that were updated, only system 26 had a drastic change in <em>z</em><sub>spec</sub> from <em>z</em><sub>26</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.1851 to <em>z</em><sub>26</sub>\u00a0=\u00a03.2355 (see Caminha et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib15\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib15\">2017</a>). In Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaacf8ef2\">2</a>, we overplot the positions of the arcs on a WFC/IR (F160W) image of MACS J0416.1-2403. The colors represent the source spectroscopic redshift, the symbols indicate if the lensed system is part of the training (plus) or new (diamond) set, and the box identifies the location of system 26.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjaacf8ef1\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaacf8ef1\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/863/1/60/Full/apjaacf8ef1_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 1.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 1.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/863/1/60/Full/apjaacf8ef1_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 1.</strong>\u00a0Redshift distribution of the background sources that are lensed by the galaxy cluster MACS J0416.1-2403. spectroscopic redshifts (<em>z</em><sub>spec</sub>) used in our analysis.</p>\n</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/863/1/60/suppdata/apjaacf8et1_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/1538-4357/aacf8e\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/0004-637X/863/1/60/suppdata/apjaacf8et1_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><p>The independent lensing teams have ranked the lensed systems based on the confidence associated with the identification of the multiple images, the availability of the spectroscopic redshift for the source, and lensing geometry. The arcs that had the highest reliability and measured spectroscopic redshifts were labeled \"GOLD.\" Secure arcs with no available <em>z</em><sub>spec</sub> were labeled \"SILVER.\" Lastly, arcs labeled \"BRONZE\" were the multiply imaged systems where there was neither unanimous agreement on the reliability nor spectroscopic redshift confirmation. The lensing teams used these vetted selections to compute the lens models. We refer to these classifications in this paper.</p></div><h3 id=\"apjaacf8es2-4\" name=\"apjaacf8es2-4\">2.4.\u00a0Lensing Models</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>The lensing groups contracted by STScI computed independent lens models using a variety of algorithms, which can generally be separated into two categories: \"parametric\" and \"non-parametric\" (also called \"free-form\"). Parametric algorithms use a parameterized density distribution for dark matter halos and cluster-member galaxies to determine the lensing potential and mass distribution of the cluster. Non-parametric or free-form algorithms make little to no assumptions regarding the functional form of the density profile of the galaxy cluster. Hybrid models are some combination of the parametric and non-parametric algorithms. In addition to the different forms of modeling the dark matter halos, an assumption that light traces mass is used in some of the algorithms.</p><p>The following is a brief overview of the models analyzed in this work. A summary of the lens model names, algorithms, and constraints can be found in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaacf8et2\">2</a>. A more detailed description of the lens models can be found on the <em>HST</em> Frontier Fields Lensing Models webpage.<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaacf8efn2\">2</a></sup>\n\n</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"apjaacf8et2\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\"><p><b>Table 2.</b>\u00a0\nHFF V3 Lens Models for MACS J0416.1-2403\n</p><table cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" border=\"0\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaacf8et2\" data-toolbar-img=\"/0004-637X/863/1/60/suppdata/apjaacf8et2_lr.gif\" data-toolbar-type=\"table\" data-toolbar-title=\"Table 2\"><colgroup><col align=\"left\"></col><col align=\"left\"></col><col align=\"left\"></col><col align=\"left\"></col><col align=\"left\"></col></colgroup><thead>\n<tr valign=\"top\">\n<th scope=\"col\" colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Lens Model</th>\n<th scope=\"col\" colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Algorithm Name</th>\n<th scope=\"col\" colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Algorithm</th>\n<th scope=\"col\" colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Constraints Used</th>\n<th scope=\"col\" colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Model Reference</th>\n</tr>\n</thead><tbody>\n<tr valign=\"top\">\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">B-V3</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">SWUnited</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Non-Parametric</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">\"GOLD\"</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Hoag et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib51\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib51\">2016</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr valign=\"top\">\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">JS-V3</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">LENSTOOL</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Parametric</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">\"GOLD\"</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Johnson et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib43\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib43\">2014</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr valign=\"top\">\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">W-V3</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">GRALE</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Non-Parametric</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">\"GOLD,\" \"SILVER\"</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Mohammed et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib69\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib69\">2014</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr valign=\"top\">\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">W-V3.1</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">GRALE</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Non-Parametric</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">\"GOLD,\" \"SILVER,\" \"BRONZE\"</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Mohammed et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib69\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib69\">2014</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr valign=\"top\">\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Z-LTM</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">LTM</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Parametric</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">\"GOLD,\" \"SILVER\"</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Broadhurst et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib14\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib14\">2005</a>), Zitrin et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib97\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib97\">2013</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr valign=\"top\">\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Z-NFW</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">PIEMD+eNFW</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Parametric</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">\"GOLD,\" \"SILVER\"</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Zitrin et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib96\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib96\">2009</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib97\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib97\">2013</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody></table><p><small>\n<p><strong>Note.</strong> This is a summary of the 10 public version 3 models of MACS J0416.1-2403, including the name, type of algorithm, and constraints used to compute the model. For definitions of the constraints, see Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaacf8es2-3\">2.3</a>.</p>\n</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/863/1/60/suppdata/apjaacf8et2_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/1538-4357/aacf8e\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/0004-637X/863/1/60/suppdata/apjaacf8et2_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><p>CATS (C-V3, C-V3.1) collaboration (Jauzac et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib39\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib39\">2012</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib38\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib38\">2014</a>; Richard et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib79\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib79\">2014</a>) and Sharon/Johnson (JS-V3) team (hereafter JS; Johnson et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib43\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib43\">2014</a>) used the publicly available parametric lensing model software <tt>LENSTOOL</tt> (Jullo et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib47\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib47\">2007</a>; Jullo &amp; Kneib <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib46\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib46\">2009</a>). JS used only strong lensing, while CATS used a combination of strong and weak lensing for the reconstruction of the mass distribution of the galaxy cluster. The total mass distribution of the cluster is parameterized by a combination of cluster-scale halos and a contribution from individual cluster-member galaxies, using scaling relations to observed galaxy properties. <tt>LENSTOOL</tt> uses a Bayesian Monte Carlo Markov Chain algorithm to explore the parameter space, minimizing a <em>\u03c7</em><sup>2</sup> to identify the best set of parameters. There are two models computed by CATS. Version 3 (C-V3) used only the \"GOLD\" and \"SILVER\" arcs, while version 3.1(C-V3.1) used \"GOLD,\" \"SILVER,\" and \"BRONZE.\" The model by JS (JS-V3) only included the \"GOLD\" arcs.</p><p>Glafic (G-V3) (Oguri <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib75\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib75\">2010</a>; Ishigaki et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib37\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib37\">2015</a>; Kawamata et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib51\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib51\">2016</a>) used a parametric algorithm in which a large smooth elliptical Navarro\u2013Frenk\u2013White (NFW; Navarro et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib72\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib72\">1997</a>) profile represents the cluster mass distribution, while the individual galaxies are modeled using Pseudo-Jaffe ellipsoids (Keeton <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib52\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib52\">2001</a>). To complement these two components, external and internal perturbations of the lensing potential were introduced and represented by a multipole Taylor expansion. The \"GOLD\" and \"SILVER\" arcs were used to constrain the lens model.</p><p>Zitrin (Z-NFW, Z-LTM) models (Zitrin et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib96\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib96\">2009</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib97\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib97\">2013</a>) used two different methods of parameterization. The first is a NFW dark matter halo density to describe the cluster mass distribution. The second method, introduced by Broadhurst et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib14\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib14\">2005</a>), is called Light-Traces-Mass (LTM). LTM uses a parametric profile for the cluster-member galaxies scaled to their luminosity, then the mass map is smoothed using a Gaussian kernel to represent the dark matter component of the cluster. Both Z-LTM and Z-NFW use the \"GOLD\" and \"SILVER\" arcs.</p><p>Brada\u010d (B-V3) (Hoag et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib34\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib34\">2016</a>) used Strong and Weak Lensing United (SWUnited Brada\u010d et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib11\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib11\">2006</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib12\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib12\">2009</a>). This non-parametric model combines both strong and weak lensing analysis to constrain the gravitational potential through iterative minimization of <em>\u03c7</em><sup>2</sup> of a non-regular adaptive grid. The \"GOLD\" arcs were used to compute the model.</p><p>Williams (W-V3, W-V3.1) models (Liesenborgs et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib60\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib60\">2006</a>; Mohammed et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib69\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib69\">2014</a>) used GRALE, a non-parametric method that uses a genetic algorithm to iteratively refine the mass distribution on a grid. The models only use the lensing observables as constraints, with no other assumption on the mass density profile or cluster galaxies. This method is ideal for testing the assumption that light traces the mass of the cluster. The W-V3 model used the \"GOLD\" and \"SILVER\" arcs, while the model W-V3.1 used \"GOLD,\" \"SILVER,\" and \"BRONZE\" arcs.</p><p>Diego (D-V3)<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaacf8efn3\">3</a></sup>\n (Diego et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib26\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib26\">2015b</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib27\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib27\">2016b</a>) used WSLAP+, which is a free-form algorithm with the addition of a parameterized distribution for the mass contribution from the galaxy cluster members. The large-scale dark matter distribution of the cluster is obtained using the non-parametric algorithm, using a superposition of two-dimensional Gaussians in an adaptive grid. The compact mass contribution from the cluster members is tied to a light-to-mass ratio. The \"GOLD\" and \"SILVER\" arcs have been used as inputs to compute the lens model.</p></div></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjaacf8es3\" name=\"apjaacf8es3\">3.\u00a0Strong Lens Models Evaluation</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>The lensing equation provides a transformation between each image location in the image plane to that of its source in the source plane:</p><div xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"display-eqn\" id=\"apjaacf8eeqn1\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/863/1/60/Full/apjaacf8eeqn1.gif\" alt=\"Equation (1)\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex; mode=display\">\\begin{eqnarray}{{\\boldsymbol{\\beta }}}_{s} & = & {{\\boldsymbol{\\theta }}}_{i}-{\\boldsymbol{\\alpha }}({{\\boldsymbol{\\theta }}}_{i}),\\\\ {\\boldsymbol{\\alpha }}({{\\boldsymbol{\\theta }}}_{i}) & = & \\displaystyle \\frac{{D}_{\\mathrm{ls}}({z}_{l},{z}_{s})}{{D}_{{\\rm{s}}}({z}_{s})}\\hat{{\\boldsymbol{\\alpha }}}({{\\boldsymbol{\\theta }}}_{i}),\\end{eqnarray}\n\t\t\t\t\\tag{\n\t\t\t\t1\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t</script></span></div><p>where <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/863/1/60/Full/apjaacf8eieqn1.gif\" alt=\"${{\\boldsymbol{\\beta }}}_{s}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{{\\boldsymbol{\\beta }}}_{s}</script></span></span> is the source plane position, <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/863/1/60/Full/apjaacf8eieqn2.gif\" alt=\"${{\\boldsymbol{\\theta }}}_{i}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{{\\boldsymbol{\\theta }}}_{i}</script></span></span> is the location in the image plane of image <em>i</em> of source <em>s</em>, <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/863/1/60/Full/apjaacf8eieqn3.gif\" alt=\"$\\hat{{\\boldsymbol{\\alpha }}}({{\\boldsymbol{\\theta }}}_{i})$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\hat{{\\boldsymbol{\\alpha }}}({{\\boldsymbol{\\theta }}}_{i})</script></span></span> is the deflection angle, <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/863/1/60/Full/apjaacf8eieqn4.gif\" alt=\"${D}_{\\mathrm{ls}}({z}_{l},{z}_{s})$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{D}_{\\mathrm{ls}}({z}_{l},{z}_{s})</script></span></span> is the angular diameter distance between the lens and the source, and <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/863/1/60/Full/apjaacf8eieqn5.gif\" alt=\"${D}_{{\\rm{s}}}({z}_{s})$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{D}_{{\\rm{s}}}({z}_{s})</script></span></span> is the angular diameter distance between the observer and the source. Lens modeling algorithms find the distribution of projected mass density that minimizes the scatter between the observed and predicted images of all background sources. Ideally, the strong lensing analysis would be done in the image plane where the observables are found, typically minimizing the equation (Kneib &amp; Natarajan <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib57\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib57\">2011</a>)</p><div xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"display-eqn\" id=\"apjaacf8eeqn2\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/863/1/60/Full/apjaacf8eeqn2.gif\" alt=\"Equation (2)\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex; mode=display\">\\begin{eqnarray}&&{\\chi }_{s}^{2}=\\displaystyle \\sum _{i=1}^{{n}_{s}}\\displaystyle \\frac{{[{{\\boldsymbol{\\theta }}}_{\\mathrm{obs}}^{i}-{{\\boldsymbol{\\theta }}}_{\\mathrm{model}}^{i}]}^{2}}{{\\delta }_{{si}}^{2}},\\end{eqnarray}\n\t\t\t\t\\tag{\n\t\t\t\t2\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t</script></span></div><p>where <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/863/1/60/Full/apjaacf8eieqn6.gif\" alt=\"${{\\boldsymbol{\\theta }}}_{\\mathrm{obs}}^{i}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{{\\boldsymbol{\\theta }}}_{\\mathrm{obs}}^{i}</script></span></span> and <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/863/1/60/Full/apjaacf8eieqn7.gif\" alt=\"${{\\boldsymbol{\\theta }}}_{\\mathrm{model}}^{i}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{{\\boldsymbol{\\theta }}}_{\\mathrm{model}}^{i}</script></span></span> are the observed and the predicted positions by the lens model of image <em>i</em> of system <em>s</em>, respectively, and <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/863/1/60/Full/apjaacf8eieqn8.gif\" alt=\"${\\delta }_{{si}}^{2}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{\\delta }_{{si}}^{2}</script></span></span> is the error on the position of image <em>i</em> in the lensed system <em>s</em>.</p><p>When assessing the image plane scatter of the different lens models for the analysis presented in this paper, we found that some models fail to predict all the multiple images for some of the systems (see Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaacf8es3-3\">3.3</a>). In those cases, the scatter of the system would be driven by the largest angular separation between the observed images in the image plane, preventing a quantitatively meaningful assessment of the models.</p><p>We overcome this issue by resorting to measuring the scatter in the source plane. Since the lens equation does not need to be inverted, there is always a prediction for <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/863/1/60/Full/apjaacf8eieqn9.gif\" alt=\"${{\\boldsymbol{\\beta }}}_{s}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{{\\boldsymbol{\\beta }}}_{s}</script></span></span>. The source plane and image plane areas are related to each other through the lensing magnification, which can be different for each of the multiple images <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/863/1/60/Full/apjaacf8eieqn10.gif\" alt=\"${{\\boldsymbol{\\theta }}}_{i}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{{\\boldsymbol{\\theta }}}_{i}</script></span></span>. We therefore average over the magnification-weighted contribution to the scatter of each image, as detailed below.</p><h3 id=\"apjaacf8es3-1\" name=\"apjaacf8es3-1\">3.1.\u00a0Source Plane Scatter per System</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>To quantify the performance of the lensing models we use the magnification-weighted rms scatter of the projected source positions in the source plane, with the goal of evaluating the predictive power of the models, and exploring its dependence on redshift and position in the image plane.</p><p>The source plane location <strong><em>\u03b2</em></strong><sub><em>i</em></sub> of each image <em>i</em> of source <em>s</em> is calculated from the lensing equation (Equation (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"eqnref\" href=\"#apjaacf8eeqn1\">1</a>)). We use the deflection matrices (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/863/1/60/Full/apjaacf8eieqn11.gif\" alt=\"$\\hat{{\\boldsymbol{\\alpha }}}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\hat{{\\boldsymbol{\\alpha }}}</script></span></span>) from the publicly released lens models, observed positions of the arcs (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/863/1/60/Full/apjaacf8eieqn12.gif\" alt=\"${{\\boldsymbol{\\theta }}}_{i}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{{\\boldsymbol{\\theta }}}_{i}</script></span></span>), and the source spectroscopic redshift data <em>z</em><sub><em>s</em></sub> (see Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaacf8et3\">3</a>). The deflection maps are interpolated using a bivariate spline. The interpolation is critical to increasing the precision when determining the location in the source plane of the multiple images.</p><p>Since the true position of the background source is non-observable, we compute the barycenter (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/863/1/60/Full/apjaacf8eieqn13.gif\" alt=\"$\\langle {{\\boldsymbol{\\beta }}}_{s}\\rangle $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\langle {{\\boldsymbol{\\beta }}}_{s}\\rangle</script></span></span>) of the projected source positions (Gade <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib32\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib32\">2010</a>), weighted by the magnification of each image:</p><div xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"display-eqn\" id=\"apjaacf8eeqn3\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/863/1/60/Full/apjaacf8eeqn3.gif\" alt=\"Equation (3)\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex; mode=display\">\\begin{eqnarray}&&\\langle {{\\boldsymbol{\\beta }}}_{s}\\rangle =\\displaystyle \\frac{{\\displaystyle \\sum }_{i=1}^{{n}_{s}}{\\mu }_{i}{{\\boldsymbol{\\beta }}}_{i}}{{\\displaystyle \\sum }_{i=1}^{{n}_{s}}{\\mu }_{i}},\\end{eqnarray}\n\t\t\t\t\\tag{\n\t\t\t\t3\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t</script></span></div><p>where <em>i</em>\u00a0=\u00a01, 2, 3, ..., <em>n</em><sub><em>s</em></sub> is the index of each image of lensed system <em>s</em>, <em>n</em><sub><em>s</em></sub> is the total number of multiple images in the system, and <em>\u03bc</em><sub><em>i</em></sub> is the magnification of image <em>i</em>. Lastly, the distances between the barycenter and source plane locations are measured using the Vincenty formulae (Vincenty <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaacf8ebib93\" id=\"fnref-apjaacf8ebib93\">1975</a>) to measure an rms scatter in the source plane. The weighted source plane rms scatter (<em>\u03c3</em><sub><em>s</em></sub>) for each of the systems is computed as follows:</p><div xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"display-eqn\" id=\"apjaacf8eeqn4\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/863/1/60/Full/apjaacf8eeqn4.gif\" alt=\"Equation (4)\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex; mode=display\">\\begin{eqnarray}&&{\\sigma }_{s}={\\left(\\displaystyle \\frac{1}{{n}_{s}^{2}}\\displaystyle \\sum _{j=1}^{{n}_{s}}\\displaystyle \\frac{1}{{\\mu }_{j}^{2}}\\displaystyle \\sum _{i=1}^{{n}_{s}}{({\\mu }_{i}| | {{\\boldsymbol{\\beta }}}_{i}-\\langle {{\\boldsymbol{\\beta }}}_{s}\\rangle | | )}^{2}\\right)}^{1/2},\\end{eqnarray}\n\t\t\t\t\\tag{\n\t\t\t\t4\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t</script></span></div><p>where the summation takes into account the different magnifications of the images.</p><p>When calculating the average scatter of several systems, <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/863/1/60/Full/apjaacf8eieqn14.gif\" alt=\"$\\overline{\\sigma }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\overline{\\sigma }</script></span></span>, we use the formula</p><div xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"display-eqn\" id=\"apjaacf8eeqn5\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/863/1/60/Full/apjaacf8eeqn5.gif\" alt=\"Equation (5)\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex; mode=display\">\\begin{eqnarray}&&\\overline{\\sigma }=\\displaystyle \\frac{1}{N}\\sum _{s}^{N}({\\sigma }_{s}),\\end{eqnarray}\n\t\t\t\t\\tag{\n\t\t\t\t5\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t</script></span></div><p>where <em>s</em>\u00a0=\u00a01, 2, 3, ..., <em>N</em> is the index of the system, <em>N</em> is the total number of systems, and <em>\u03c3</em><sub><em>s</em></sub> is the source plane scatter of system <em>s</em> (Equation (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"eqnref\" href=\"#apjaacf8eeqn4\">4</a>)).</p><p>We note that even though all of the modelers used the same list of multiple images (as described in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaacf8es2-3\">2.3</a>), the positions are slightly altered; for example, they may use a unique morphological feature or a bright clump in the arc as the positional constraint. The coordinates used in this paper are tabulated in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaacf8et3\">3</a>. We tested whether the exact choice of coordinate within the arc affects the results of our analysis. We computed the percent difference in the source plane scatter between two sets of positional coordinates from two different lensing teams.<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaacf8efn4\">4</a></sup>\n We find that the source plane rms scatter changes by less than 5% between the coordinate sets. This test provides confidence that the results described in the following sections are robust to slight differences in the coordinates used by the different teams.</p><h4 id=\"apjaacf8es3-1-1\" name=\"apjaacf8es3-1-1\">3.1.1.\u00a0General Results</h4><div class=\"article-text\"><p>In Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaacf8ef3\">3</a>, we plot the rms scatter (<em>\u03c3</em><sub><em>s</em></sub>) for each system for all the lens models, and in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaacf8ef4\">4</a> we show the distributions (represented by <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/863/1/60/Full/apjaacf8eieqn15.gif\" alt=\"$\\overline{\\sigma }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\overline{\\sigma }</script></span></span>, first, and third quartiles) of the system rms scatter of the training set, new set, and combined set, for a more direct comparison between the models.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjaacf8ef3\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaacf8ef3\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/863/1/60/Full/apjaacf8ef3_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 3.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 3.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/863/1/60/Full/apjaacf8ef3_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 3.</strong>\u00a0The system rms scatter for each lensed source (<em>\u03c3</em><sub><em>s</em></sub>, Equation (<a class=\"eqnref\" href=\"#apjaacf8eeqn4\">4</a>)) is plotted against the arc systems. The filled circles represent the systems that are part of the training set, and the open circles represent systems that are part of the new set. The arrows at the top of the graph indicate data points that have a scatter &gt; 2<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />0. The blue \"x\" represents the average scatter of the training systems and new systems, respectively, for each model (<span class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/863/1/60/Full/apjaacf8eieqn16.gif\" alt=\"$\\overline{\\sigma }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\overline{\\sigma }</script></span></span>, Equation (<a class=\"eqnref\" href=\"#apjaacf8eeqn5\">5</a>)). The red dot marks system 26, whose redshift has been updated.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjaacf8ef3\" href=\"/0004-637X/863/1/60/downloadFigure/figure/apjaacf8ef3\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjaacf8ef3\" href=\"/0004-637X/863/1/60/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjaacf8ef3\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjaacf8ef4\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaacf8ef4\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/863/1/60/Full/apjaacf8ef4_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 4.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden;
